[1] Chapter 1: Anthony Ked is hired on the spot
[2] "Mr. Jolly!"
[3] "Jimmy McGregor?"
[4] The seven ladies of the Jazzy High-End Tour Group looked gloomy, and the three men were already sweating. They watched with interest, however, as Ked met an old friend. Ked was the tour guide for the group, much loved by the tourists. He was tall and thin, with dark skin and a quick wit, adept at mediating disputes and calming nerves. His friend, however, seemed a bit odd. He was about the same height as Ked, but much broader and far less handsome.
[5] He looked like the kind of bar owner described in books. It was interesting, though, as the purpose of the tour was to see what the books described. At this moment, the entire group was bored with Bravaio [1], the sun was unbearable, and the hotel was uncomfortable. There was nothing to do but wait for the drive to Matopos. Luckily, Mr. Ked suggested looking at postcards, and there were plenty to choose from.
[6] Anthony Ked and his friend moved a few steps away.
[7] "What are you doing with a bunch of women?" McGregor asked. "Harem of a thousand beauties?"
[8] "Not enough!" Anthony grinned. "You should look around."
[9] "I did, and your taste is terrible."
[10] "My taste is as good as ever. This is the Jazzy High-End Tour Group, and I am the tour guide for Jazzy Travel."
[11] "How did you get into this line of work?"
[12] "I had no choice, I needed money. But this job isn't really my thing."
[13] Jimmy chuckled.
[14] "Always off the beaten path, right?"
[15] Anthony didn't take his words to heart.
[16] "It's all about bouncing back," Anthony said hopefully.
[17] Jimmy chuckled softly.
[18] "I know you're always in the middle of trouble, Anthony Kidd. You're just a magnet for it. And you're like a cat with nine lives, not afraid to die. When do you have time to chat?"
[19] Anthony sighed.
[20] "I have to take these chatty hens to the Rozz Graveyard."
[21] "That's the spirit," Jimmy said approvingly, "They'll be all bruised and battered from the rough roads, and they'll be whining about needing to rest in bed. Then, we can go out for a couple of drinks and chat."
[22] "Great, see you later!"
[23] Anthony returned to the tour group, and the youngest and most frivolous Miss Taylor immediately made her move.
[24] "Mr. Kidd, is that your old friend?"
[25] "Yes, Miss Taylor. An old friend from my youth."
[26] Miss Taylor chuckled.
[27] "He's quite interesting-looking."
[28] "I'll pass that along to him."
[29] "Oh, Mr. Cade, you're so naughty! Always with the funny ideas. What did he call you?"
[30] "Mr. Cox."
[31] "You're Cox?"
[32] "Miss Taylor, I thought you knew I was Anthony."
[33] "Go away!" Miss Taylor pouted and shrieked.
[34] Now, Anthony was getting the hang of this job. In addition to arranging the necessary travel details, his responsibilities included: carefully consoling an irate old gentleman who had been offended, providing ample time for an elderly woman who wanted postcards, and flirting with women under forty. The last task was easier, as the women were always quick to pick up on the romantic undertones in his words.
[35] Miss Taylor didn't let him off the hook.
[36] "Why does he call you 'Joe Gentleman'?"
[37] "Because it's not my name."
[38] "Why does he call you 'Joe Gentleman'?"
[39] "For the same reason."

[42] "We all think you're quite a gentleman."
[43] "I'm flattered."
[44] "I mean it."
[45] "A kind heart is more precious than a crown." Anthony mumbled incoherently, not knowing what he meant, wishing only to reach lunchtime.
[46] "I've always found this poem to be particularly beautiful. Do you know a lot of poetry, Mr. Kade?"
[47] "I can recite a couple of lines: 'A boy stands on a burning deck; The rest are gone, save he alone.' That's all I know, but I can also do some actions with it: 'A boy stands on a burning deck' (breathes in) (breathes out) (gestures, showing fire) 'The rest are gone, save he alone,' and then I run around like a dog."
[48] Miss Taylor laughed sharply.
[49] "Look at Mr. Kade! He's so funny!"
[50] "It's time for tea," Anthony said, his tone lightening up, "this way. There's a great café just down the street."
[51] "So," Mrs. Gowan asks in a deep voice, "is the tea included in the tour fee?"
[52] "Mrs. Gowan," Anthony adopts a business-like tone, "breakfast is self-paid."
[53] "What a shame!"
[54] "Life is difficult," Anthony says with a placid expression.
[55] Mrs. Gowan's eyes light up, and she exudes a sense of pride, "I knew that was coming. So, I filled my water bottle with tea this morning. I'll just heat it up with an alcohol lamp later. Come on, old man!" The Gowan couple strutted off towards the hotel, her back radiating a glow of self-satisfaction for her foresight.
[56] "What a mess!" Anthony muttered under his breath, "There are all kinds of birds in the woods!"
[57] He led the rest of the tourists to the café, with Miss Taylor walking beside him and continuing her questioning.
[58] "How long has it been since you and your friend last saw each other?"

[68] "Give me a drink, James [2]." Kidd pleaded, "I really need one."
[69] "I don't think so, man. I'd never do your kind of work."

[72] "What?"
[73] "If you can find another job, will you quit this one?"
[74] "What? You actually have a job opening? Why don't you take it yourself?"

[77] "Is there something wrong? Just because they won't let you teach at the Sunday school?"

[85] "Brother, you've said all this before. But, this job isn't in South America; it's in Britain."
[86] "Britain? After all these years abroad, are you going to return home? Won't they come after you for the debt from seven years ago?"
[87] "I don't think so. So, should I continue with this job?"
[88] "Of course. But I don't understand why you don't just do it yourself?"
[89] "I'll tell you, Anthony. I'm going to go to the interior of the country to dig for gold."
[90] Anthony whistled and stared at him.
[91] "Ever since I met you, you've always been mining for gold, Jimmy. That's your weakness, and it's also your special hobby. You're the most gold-crazy person I know."
[92] "This thing will definitely work out, you'll see."
[93] "Everyone has their own hobbies. I like to fight, and you like gold mines."
[94] "Let me tell you from the beginning, you should know about Heslovsky, right?"
[95] Hearing this, Anthony jerked his head up.
[96] "Herskovitz?" he asked curiously.
[97] "Yeah, you know about it, right?"
[98] Anthony hesitated for a moment before slowly saying, "What I know is what everyone knows: it's one of the countries in the Balkan Peninsula; its main rivers, unknown; its main mountains, unknown, just countless. The capital is Ecauste. The main population consists of bandits; their hobby is assassinating kings and staging revolutions. The last king, Nicholas IV, was assassinated about seven years ago, and then that wild place became a republic. In short, it's a place where riots are easy to happen, and you mentioned that Herskovitz had a revolution."
[99] "I didn't say that directly."
[100] Anthony stared at him, angry and mostly regretful.
[101] "You have to put some effort into this," Anthony said. "Do some research, if you were to tell such a story in the old Eastern dynasties, you would have been tied up, upside down, beaten, and tortured."
[102] Jimmy didn't take Anthony's words to heart and continued with his self-talk.
[103] "Have you heard of Count Stapfitch?"
[104] "You finally got to the point," Anthony said. "Many people may not have heard of Hesoslovakia, but they certainly know Count Stapfitch. He is a big figure in the Balkan Peninsula, the greatest politician of the contemporary era, the biggest villain, yet he was not hanged. His image varies greatly in different newspapers, but one thing is certain: Count Stapfitch's name will be remembered forever. For the past twenty years, Count Stapfitch has been the true mastermind behind every political movement and resistance activity in the Near East. He is a dictator, a patriot, and a politician all in one. Everyone knows he is a conspirator, but no one knows what kind of person he really is. By the way, why did you bring him up?"
[105] "Because he used to be the Prime Minister of Hesoslovakia."
[106] "It's not even comparable, Herscovitz is like a drop in the ocean compared to Count Stapleton. It's just his hometown and workplace. I thought he was dead, anyway."
[107] "He is dead. He died about two months ago in Paris. I'm talking about something that happened a few years ago."
[108] "What exactly are you going to tell me?"
[109] Jimmy quickly continued, "Here's what happened. Four years ago, I was in Paris. One evening, I was walking through a quiet neighborhood when I saw five or six French thugs beating up an elderly gentleman who looked quite respectable. I hate seeing people being bullied, so I intervened and beat up the thugs badly."
[110] "Good job, James," Anthony's tone softened. "I wish I could have seen that scene."
[111] "No big deal," James said modestly, "The old gentleman was very grateful. He was probably drunk that day, but he still asked for my name and address, saying he would come to thank me seriously the next day. It was then that I realized that the old man I had saved was Count Stapleton, who was hiding near the Po River at the time."
[112] Anthony nodded.
[113] "After the assassination of King Nikolai, Count Stapleton settled in Paris. Later, someone asked him to return to his country to become president. But he refused. He publicly supported constitutional monarchy, but it was rumored that he was involved in all the secret political actions on the Balkan Peninsula. Count Stapleton is too cunning."
[114] "So, Nikolai IV had a unique taste in choosing his wife, right?" James suddenly changed the topic.
[115] "Yeah." Anthony said, "He ruined himself with this, and it's a pity! The girl was the illegitimate daughter of a chorus girl in a Paris music hall, not even worthy of being considered a noble, but Nikolai fell in love with her and she insisted on being the queen. It sounds like a fairy tale, but they actually made it happen. He claimed she was a countess Popovsky or something and had the blood of the Romanov tsars. They held their wedding in the Church of Ekaterinburg, forcing several archbishops to marry them. Then, the wild girl was crowned as the Empress Farajia. Nikolai gathered a few ministers, thinking everything would be fine, but he ignored the common people. The people of Herskovitz were conservative and believed in aristocratic rule, thinking that the king and queen should be true aristocrats. There was widespread resentment, and the authorities cruelly suppressed it, which eventually led to a major uprising, where the people stormed the palace, killed the king and queen, and proclaimed a republic. And that's how it has been ever since. But I've heard that the situation is still not stable, and they've assassinated one or two presidents, possibly to keep up their assassination skills. Back to the story, you were talking about Count Stapleton coming to thank your savior, and then what happened?"
[116] "That's the end of the story. I forgot about it when I went back to Africa. But about two weeks ago, I received a very strange package. It was delivered to me from where I passed through, and I don't know how long it took. I saw in the newspaper that Count Stapleton recently passed away in Paris. The package contained his autobiography, or memoirs, or whatever. There was also a letter saying that if I could deliver the manuscript to a publisher in London by October 13th or before, I would receive £1,000."
[117] "A thousand pounds? You mean a thousand pounds, Jimmy?"
[118] "Yes, a thousand pounds, man. I hope it's not a scam. As the saying goes, the words of kings and politicians cannot be trusted. So what should I do with this? The package has been following me, and I can't delay it any longer. Unfortunately, I have already booked a trip to the interior of Africa, and this opportunity is rare and cannot be missed. I have made up my mind."
[119] "You're hopeless. Two birds in the forest are not as good as one in hand."
[120] "What if it's a scam? Anyway, I have already booked a ticket to Cape Town, and everything is arranged. Fate brought you here."
[121] Anthony stood up and lit a cigarette.
[122] "I understand your point, James. You go ahead with your gold dig and I'll collect the thousand pounds for you. So, what's in it for me?"
[123] "A quarter, how about that?"
[124] "Conventionally, a quarter of a thousand pounds, tax-free, right?"
[125] "Yes!"
[126] "Alright! I'm done. You might hate me for this, but I'll do it for a hundred pounds. James McGregor, you just can't seem to save any money."
[127] "Whatever, is it a deal?"
[128] "Deal, I agree! So, the Jasper Traveling Group will be in chaos."
[129] The two of them clinked their glasses solemnly.

[134] Chapter 2: The Troubled Woman
[135] "So, that's settled!" Anthony drained his glass and placed it on the table. "Which ship are you taking?"
[136] "The Granada."
[137] "You booked under your name, so I'll go as James McGregor. No problems with the passport?"
[138] "Either name will do. Although we don't look alike at all, we do share some obvious physical features: six feet tall, brown hair, blue eyes; nose, ordinary; chin, ordinary…"
[139] "Cut out the 'ordinary' talk. I'll have you know I was handpicked for the Jasper Travel Team, and it was all thanks to my handsome looks and graceful manners."
[140] Jimmy grinned.
[141] "I saw your graceful demeanor this morning."
[142] "Go away!"
[143] Anthony stands up and paces around the room. He furrows his brow for a few minutes before speaking:
[144] "Jimmy," he says, "why did the Count of Stapleton send a manuscript to London via Africa after his death in Paris?"
[145] Jimmy shakes his head in confusion.
[146] "I don't know."
[147] "Why not just wrap it up and mail it?"
[148] "That sounds more reasonable."
[149] "Of course," Anthony continued, "I know that kings, queens, and government officials are supposed to do things in a certain way out of courtesy, which is why there are things like royal messengers. In the Middle Ages, they would give a seal ring as a kind of spell to open doors. 'This is the king's ring! Let me pass!' Usually, the ring was stolen. I just don't understand why no one has ever thought to make a fake ring or even ten or eight of them, selling each for a hundred ducats[1]. Middle Ages people are so dull."
[150] Jimmy yawned as he listened.
[151] "Your comments about the Middle Ages don't seem to interest you. Let's talk about the Earl of Stapleton instead. It's quite foolish for a diplomat to send something from France to Africa and then to England. If he really wanted you to have the thousand pounds, he should have put it in his will. Fortunately, neither of us is so proud as to refuse a bequest. Stapleton is really crazy."
[152] "Do you really think so?"
[153] Anthony furrowed his brow and continued pacing around the room.
[154] "Have you seen that thing?" he suddenly asked.
[155] "What thing?"
[156] "That manuscript."
[157] "What on earth for? I don't see the point in looking at that thing."
[158] Anthony smiled.
[159] "I was just wondering. You know, there are often troubles caused by biographies and revelations. It seems that people who are silent for most of their lives like to stir up some trouble when they die, feeling a kind of malicious satisfaction. Jimmy, what kind of person is Lord Steppendale? You've met him, talked to him, and you're good at judging people. Do you think he's like a vengeful old devil?"
[160] Jimmy shook his head.
[161] "It's hard to say. You see, he was drunk the first night; the next day, he turned into a noble old man, polite and flattering to the point of making me feel embarrassed."
[162] "Did he say anything special when he was drunk?"
[163] Jimmy furrowed his brow, recalling the situation.
[164] "He said he knows where the Light Mountain Diamond is."
[165] "Well...," Anthony said, "everyone knows that the diamond is displayed in the Tower of London's exhibition room, under a thick glass case, guarded by iron bars, and surrounded by well-dressed people."
[166] "That's right." Jimmy agreed.
[167] "Did Stapleton mention anything else like that? For example, he knew where Wallace was hiding it in a city."
[168] Jimmy shook his head.
[169] "Uh...," Anthony replied, then lit a cigarette and paced back and forth.
[170] "You probably never read the papers, you uncultured swine." After a moment, he asked.
[171] "Not too often," McGregor answered simply. "There's not much in the paper that interests me."
[172] "Fortunately, I'm more civilized than you. There have been frequent mentions of Heslovich in the papers lately, which could be a sign that the monarchy is making a comeback."
[173] "But Nicholas IV has no heirs," Jimmy said. "But I always feel that the House of Opolovitch is not yet extinct, with young blood flowing in, like cousins, distant cousins, and even more distant cousins."
[174] "So, finding a heir to the throne is not difficult?"
[175] "Not at all," Jimmy answered. "If they ever get tired of the republic, I wouldn't be surprised. Those tough guys are used to assassinating kings, and shooting a president just doesn't have the same thrill or challenge. As for kings, I just remembered something Steptoe said that night, that he knew the thugs who attacked him, they were from Viktor's court."
[176] "What?" Anthony whirled around.
[177] McGrath's mouth curved into a wider smile.
[178] "Getting excited, Mr. Gents?" he drawled.
[179] "Be serious, Jimmy. This is quite important."
[180] He walked over to the window and stood there, gazing out.
[181] "Who's Victor King?" Jimmy asked. "Another royal family from a Balkan country?"
[182] "No," Anthony said slowly. "He's not that kind of king."
[183] "Then who is he?"
[184] Anthony paused for a moment before saying, "Jimmy, he's a con artist, a notorious jewel thief, and a brazen one at that. Victor King is just a codename he used in Paris. Paris is his gang's headquarters, and that's where he was caught. But they couldn't find enough evidence for his heavy crimes, so they gave him a light sentence of seven years. He's probably out by now, or maybe already has been."
[185] "Do you think Count Stapleton's imprisonment has anything to do with him? Were those thugs following him for revenge?"
[186] "I don't know," Anthony said. "It doesn't seem like it on the surface. As far as I know, Victor King hasn't touched the Hessian royal family. But it all looks so suspicious, doesn't it? Count Stapleton's death, that memoir, the rumors in the papers – everything is vague and intriguing. And I've also heard that Hessia has discovered oil. James, I have a strong feeling that they've been eyeing that insignificant little country."
[187] "Who?"
[188] "The Hebrews, the yellow-faced financial moguls sitting in their offices."
[189] "So, what's your point?"
[190] "Just making things complicated, that's all."
[191] "Not that," Anthony said, slightly disappointed. "Guess where I'm planning to go with those two hundred and fifty pounds?"
[192] "South America?"
[193] "No, I'm going to Hesslovia. I think I could stand with that republic, and maybe even become its president."
[194] "Why don't you just claim to be a descendant of the Paulovich bloodline and go there to be a king?"
[195] "No, James. A king has to reign for life, while a president only serves for four years. For me, a country like Hesslovia, four years is just right."
[196] "A king might not even last four years," Jimmy interjected.
[197] "I might not be able to resist taking a thousand pounds from your share. By the time you've brought back the gold, a thousand pounds won't even be a blip on your radar. So, I'll invest it in Hersovlav's oil mines. You know, James? This idea just keeps getting better and better. I never would have thought of Hersovlav if you hadn't mentioned it. I'll spend a day in London, grab the thousand pounds, and then catch the Balkan Express."
[198] "Don't rush off so quickly. I actually have something else I want you to do for me."
[199] Anthony sat down on the chair, looking serious.
[200] "I always felt like there was something else, and sure enough, it's all coming together."
[201] "It's nothing like that. I just want you to do a small favor for a lady."
[202] "Not a chance. I'm not getting involved in your love affairs."
[203] "It's not like that. I haven't even met the woman. Let me tell you the whole story."
[204] "If you're going to ramble on, I'll have to have another drink."
[205] The host hastened to oblige, and then began to relate the tale.
[206] "It happened in Uganda. I saved a South European man…"
[207] "James, if I were you, I'd write a book called 'The People I've Saved.' This is the second story I've heard tonight."
[208] "This time, I didn't do much. I just pulled him out of the river. It seems that most South Europeans can't swim."
[209] "Wait, is this related to something else?"
[210] "No, not really. But I just remembered something strange. Although we call him Pedro, which is a Dutch name, he's actually from Hesse."
[211] Anthony nodded indifferently, "It doesn't matter what you call him, they're all South Europeans. Go on."
[212] "The guy might have been grateful, so he followed me like a dog. About six months later, he died of a fever. Before he passed away, he called me over and whispered a secret in my ear using some jargon, I thought he was talking about a gold mine, then he shoved a small oilcloth package into my hand. Well, I didn't take it seriously at the time. It wasn't until a week later that I opened the package. I admit, I was just too curious. I knew that with Pedro's intelligence, even if he saw a gold mine, he might not recognize it, but what if it was really a gold mine?"
[213] "The thought of gold must have made your heart race, it's hard to resist," Anthony interrupted him.
[214] "I've never felt so disgusted in my life. Gold mine? Ha. For that scumbag, that thing could have been a gold mine. Do you know what it was? A letter from a woman, yes, a British woman. The bitch was blackmailing another woman, and she had the nerve to give me that filthy thing."
[215] "Your integrity is admirable, James, but South Europeans are South Europeans. His intentions were good. You saved his life, so he left his livelihood for you."
[216] "What am I supposed to do with this thing? Burn it? That's what I thought at first, but then I thought about that poor woman who wouldn't know the letters were destroyed and would be living in constant fear of that South European showing up again."
[217] "I never thought you had such an imaginative mind." Anthony said, lighting a cigarette, "You're right, that makes it more complicated. Should we mail it to her?"
[218] "Like most women, she didn't leave dates or addresses on most of the letters, but there was one with what looked like an address information, but only a name: Chimney Cottage."
[219] Anthony was about to blow out the match in his hand when he suddenly froze, only to flick it away when the flame burned his fingers.
[220] "Chimney Cottage?" he said. "That's too bizarre."
[221] "Do you know it?"
[222] "Darling, it's a British mansion, where the king and queen often spend weekends, and diplomats gather there."
[223] "I'd rather you go to England than me, because you know all about these things. I'm just a Canadian country bumpkin who would make a mess of things. You're worldly, you've been to Eton and Harrow…"
[224] "Only Eton." Anthony said modestly.
[225] "Someone like you could handle this. You were asking me why I didn't just mail them to her? I thought it was too dangerous. I suspect her husband is jealous. What if he accidentally opened them? Or maybe the woman is dead, because the letters seem quite old. I think the only proper thing to do is to take those letters to England and hand them to her personally."
[226] Anthony dropped his cigarette and walked over to his friend, patting him affectionately on the back.
[227] "You're a real knight in shining armor, Jimmy," he said. "Your little Canadian town should be proud of you. If I were in your shoes, I wouldn't do half as well."
[228] "So you're agreeing?"
[229] "Of course."
[230] McGregor stood up, walked over to the drawer, took out a packet of letters, and dropped them on the table.
[231] "Here, you better take a look at these first."
[232] "Do I really need to?"
[233] "Based on what you told me about the chimney house, she probably just stayed there for a while. We should go through these letters and see if we can find any clues to figure out where she really lives."
[234] "I agree with you."
[235] They carefully went through all the letters, but found nothing. Anthony thoughtfully gathered the letters together.
[236] "Poor thing," he said, "she must have been terrified."
[237] Jimmy nodded.
[238] "Do you think you can find her?" he asked, worriedly.
[239] "I'll stay in Britain if I can't find her. You seem to care a lot about this stranger, James."
[240] Jimmy absent-mindedly stroked the signature on the letter.
[241] "Her name is lovely," he explained. "Her name is Virginia Ruff."

[244] Chapter Three: The Troubles of the Upper Class
[245] "Indeed, my friend, indeed," the Earl of Carrington said, dismissively.
[246] The Earl of Carrington, Edward Alastair Brent, was the ninth Earl of Carrington. He was short and shabbily dressed, looking nothing like a nobleman. His eyes were pale blue, and his long, narrow nose gave him a somewhat melancholy appearance. His manners, while somewhat stiff, were impeccable.
[247] For the ninth Earl of Carrington, the greatest misfortune of his life was inheriting his brother's title four years ago. The previous Earl had been a household name in England, a prominent figure in the government, and a key player in the British Parliament. His country estate, the Smokestack Villa, was renowned for its hospitality. His wife, the daughter of the Duke of Posh, had played a big part in that. There were always informal gatherings at the Smokestack Villa on weekends, where glasses were raised and deals were made and broken. The who's who of British and European aristocracy had all spent time there.
[248] All of that was well and good, but the ninth Earl of Carrington couldn't help but feel a sense of awe when he thought of his brother, Henry, who had done all of that. The ninth Earl simply disagreed with the idea of Smokestack Villa being considered a national asset rather than a private country house. He hated it when non-politicians talked politics, which is why George Romax's incessant prattle was so irritating. Romax was a robust man, slightly overweight, with a ruddy complexion and bulging eyes that exuded an air of self-importance.
[249] "Do you understand what I mean, Carrington? We simply cannot afford any scandal at this point. The situation is delicate," Romax said.
[250] "You understand my meaning, Carrington? We cannot afford any scandal at this point. The situation is delicate."
[251] "Always has been." Lord Carrington replied with a touch of sarcasm.
[252] "I'm a man of action, Carrington."
[253] "Indeed, indeed." Lord Carrington reverted to his previous tactic.
[254] "If there is any mistake in Hesslovakia, we are done for. The most important thing is to grant the oil drilling rights to a British company. Please pay attention, will you?"
[255] "Of course, of course."
[256] "Prince Michael O'Paulwich arrives this weekend, organizing a hunting party at the Chimney House to provide a cover, and the whole thing will be wrapped up."

[406] Whitehall is a street in the City of London that connects the House of Commons and Downing Street. Along this street and nearby are located the Ministry of Defence, the Foreign and Commonwealth Office, the Home Office, and the Admiralty, among other British government departments. Therefore, "Whitehall" is often used as a synonym for the British civil service.
[407] Chapter 5: The First Night in London

[762] "Absolutely. Now I'm just thinking about quickly getting the manuscript copied a few times, so that even if the original is destroyed, it won't be a big loss."
[763] "My goodness!" said Anthony.
[764] "I know it sounds ridiculous to you. But you really don't understand the current situation. There are people trying to prevent us from getting the manuscript, and they don't want us to have it. And I'm being honest with you, if you want to bring the manuscript yourself, you probably won't make it here."
[765] "I don't believe it." said Anthony. "I can do whatever I want to do."
[766] "You're facing a very dangerous group of people. A month ago, I didn't believe it either. I'm telling you, Mr. McGregor, people have been bribing, threatening, and manipulating us to get that manuscript. I suggest you don't bring the manuscript yourself. I'll send someone to your hotel to pick it up."
[767] "What if that person gets taken care of?" Anthony asked.
[768] "That's on us, not on you. You just give it to our person, and they'll give you a written statement. We agreed with the late... uh... author, you know who, that we should pay you £1,000. It will be sent to you as a check next Wednesday. But if you insist on receiving the money first, I can write you a check for the same amount, and have that person bring it to you."
[769] Anthony thought for a moment. He had planned to wait until the last minute to bring the manuscript, as he wanted to see what was so shocking about it. But he realized the publisher had a valid point.
[770] "Alright." He sighed softly. "Do as you say. Send someone over. And bring the check, as I might leave Britain before next Wednesday."
[771] "Certainly, Mr. McGrath. Our person will come to you first thing tomorrow morning. I think it would be best if he doesn't come from the office. Mr. Holmes of our company lives in the south of London, and he can stop by your place on his way to work. He will bring you a receipt. I suggest you put a fake manuscript in the hotel manager's safe tonight to confuse things. If your enemies get wind of this, they won't raid your room tonight."
[772] "Okay, I'll do that," Anthony said thoughtfully, hanging up the phone.
[773] He then resumed his interrupted plan to find out more about the cunning Giuseppe. But he found nothing. Giuseppe had worked in that restaurant, but no one knew anything about his personal life or social circle.
[774] "I'll find you, you little son of a gun," Anthony growled to himself. "I'll find you, sooner or later."
[775] The second night in London was very quiet. At 9 a.m. the next morning, Mr. Holmes of Packerton Haggard Publishers was led upstairs. He was short, fair-haired, and not very talkative. Anthony handed him the manuscript, and received a check for £1,000 in return. Mr. Holmes put the manuscript in his brown bag, wished Anthony good morning, and left. Everything went smoothly.
[776] "But he might have been killed on the way," Anthony said to himself, staring out the window, "I'm so curious, so curious."
[777] He put the check in an envelope, wrote a few lines on it, and sealed it carefully. Jimmy had given Anthony a large sum of money when they met in Blavet, so the money was still untouched.
[778] "One thing down, another to go," Anthony thought to himself, "I messed up on this one, but never say die! I can change my identity and check out 487 Pound Street."
[779] He packed his bags, checked out of the hotel, and instructed the bellboy to put his luggage in a taxi. Although the hotel staff hadn't done much to make him feel comfortable, he still tipped them. As the taxi was about to depart, a boy ran down the stairs and handed him a letter.
[780] "Sir, this just arrived for you." Anthony sighed and gave him another penny. The taxi roared, leaped forward, and moved off with a loud clatter of gears. Anthony opened the letter.
[781] It was a strange document that he read four times to understand. Essentially (the letter was not written in simple terms but in the unique style of government correspondence), they believed that Mr. McGlashan arrived in Britain from South Africa on Thursday. It vaguely mentioned the memoirs of the Earl of Stapleton and requested that he not act until he had spoken in confidence with Mr. George Romax and others, all of whom were implied to be very important figures. The letter explicitly invited him to visit the Chimney House as the guest of the Earl of Chatham the following day, Friday.
[782] It was a mysterious and cryptic way of expressing himself, but Anthony liked it.
[783] "Old England," he murmured with affection, "always half a step behind the times, it's a shame. Although I've been looking for a convenient hotel, I can't just waltz into Chimney House under the name of Anthony Kede."
[784] He leaned out the window and indicated a few new directions to the driver, who snorted in disdain.
[785] The taxi stopped at a secluded inn, but the driver charged him as if he were a hotel guest.
[786] He booked a room under the name of Anthony Kidd and then went into a dimly lit office. He took out a sheet of paper with the letterhead of the Blitz Hotel and hastily wrote a letter.
[787] He explained that he had arrived on Tuesday of the previous week and had already handed over the manuscript mentioned in the letter to the Puddleby-Haggick Publishing House. He regretfully declined the Earl of Carringham's invitation, as he was about to leave Britain. Finally, he signed the letter "Jimmy McGregor."
[788] "Now," Anthony said to himself as he stuck on the stamp, "it's time to get down to business. Jimmy McGregor exits, Anthony Kidd takes the stage."
[789] Chapter Eight: A Dead Man
[790] On the same Thursday afternoon, Virginia Rue was playing tennis in Ranelagh. On her way back to Pound Street, she leaned back in the limousine and rehearsed her role in the upcoming conversation. Of course, the blackmailer might not appear again, but she felt he would. In their previous encounters, she had deliberately portrayed herself as a simple-minded fool. This time, she intended to catch him off guard.
[791] The car pulled up to the house, and she chatted with the driver before climbing the steps.
[792] "Walton, I almost forgot to ask, how's your wife doing?"
[793] "She's much better, ma'am. The doctor will check on her around six-thirty. Will you need the car again?"
[794] Virginia considered for a moment.
[795] "I'm leaving for the weekend. I have to leave Paddington at six forty. But you don't need to come, I'll just call a taxi. It would be better for you to see the doctor. If the doctor thinks it's good for your wife to get out and about this weekend, you can take her out. The expenses are on me."
[796] The driver thanked her profusely, and Virginia impatiently nodded and ran up the stairs. She rummaged through her bag for a while, realizing she had forgotten her key when she left, and quickly pressed the doorbell.
[797] The person inside did not answer immediately, and while she waited, a young man walked up the stairs. He was dressed modestly and held a bundle of brochures. He handed her one, which clearly read "Why Should I Serve My Country?" in bold letters, and he also held a collection box in his left hand.

[801] "Where's Chifford?" she asked sternly as she walked into the hallway.

[803] "Who are the others? Where did they go?"

[806] "You didn't send a telegram? No, it was just an hour ago."
[807] "I never sent a telegram. What did it say?"
[808] "It should still be on the table."

[812] The telegram seemed completely ordinary, just like the one Alice had sent out spontaneously to host a gathering at the Riverside Villa. She often took the entire staff with her, leaving only an old maid behind to watch the house. Chiffers thought nothing of it and simply carried out his duties as a loyal servant.
[813] "I stayed behind," Alice explained. "I knew ma'am needed me to pack her bags."
[814] "This is a ridiculous prank," Virginia exclaimed, angrily throwing the telegram to the ground. "Alice, you know I'm going to the Chimney Villa, I told you this morning."
[815] "I thought ma'am changed her mind," Alice replied. "Isn't that what usually happens?"
[816] Virginia had no response and reluctantly gave up. All she wanted to know was why someone would pull such an unusual prank. Alice proposed a theory.
[817] "My goodness!" she exclaimed, clasping her hands together. "What if it's a bad person? They sent a fake telegram, got rid of the servants, and then they could rob us."
[818] "I think it's very likely," Virginia said suspiciously.
[819] "Yes, yes, ma'am, it must be. There are reports like that in the newspapers every day. You must call the police right away, or they'll come and cut our throats when it's too late."
[820] "Don't be so dramatic, they won't come and cut our throats at six o'clock in the afternoon."
[821] "Ma'am, please let me go out and call the police right now."
[822] "Why? Don't be silly, Alice. If you haven't packed the luggage for the smokehouse villa yet, go ahead and prepare it. Pack the new Giallo evening gown, the white silk gown, and the black silk gown. The black silk gown would be perfect for a political party, wouldn't it?"
[823] "Ma'am, the green evening gown would be the most charming!"
[824] "No, I'm not taking that one. Hurry up, Alice. We don't have much time. I'll send a telegram to Chiffers in Datchet. When we leave, also tell the patrolling police to keep an eye on this place. [825] Alice let out a piercing scream and quickly ran upstairs, glancing nervously around as she went.
[826] Virginia made a face at her back and walked through the hall to the small study. The phone was in the study, and Alice's suggestion to call the police seemed like a good idea, so she decided to do it without delay.
[827] She opened the study door and walked over to the phone. As she put her hand on the receiver, she stopped. She had forgotten all about the waiting guest, so engrossed had she been in her own worries. He must have fallen asleep while waiting for her.
[828] She smiled mischievously as she walked over to the chair. But her smile disappeared.
[829] The man was not asleep, but dead.
[830] There was a small hole, the size of a fingernail, in the man's heart, and blood was seeping out in a dark red color; his chin was hanging down, and he looked terrifying; a gleaming small gun lay on the floor. But Virginia had already sensed what had happened instinctively before she saw all this.
[831] She stood there blankly, her hands pressed tightly against her sides. In the silence, she heard Alice's footsteps down the stairs.
[832] "Ma'am, ma'am."
[833] "What? What's wrong?"
[834] She rushed to the door, at this moment, her instinct was that she must not let Alice know what had happened, otherwise she would immediately become hysterical. She knew very well that the most important thing now was to stay calm and consider what to do next.
[835] "Ma'am, should I pull up the security chain on the front door right away? The bad guys could come at any time."
[836] "Okay, do as you say."
[837] The sound of the chain rattling filled the air, and then she heard Alice running back upstairs, finally allowing her to exhale.
[838] She looked at the man in the chair and then at the phone. She knew exactly what she had to do - she needed to call the police right away.
[839] But she didn't do it, instead standing there dumbfounded, her heart racing and her mind in turmoil. The fake telegram! Were these two things related? What if Alice hadn't left? She would have come in herself (assuming she had her key, as she usually did), and then there would have been only her and the victim, or the person she had been blackmailed by before. She could explain, but the thought of that explanation made her even more uneasy. Even George would find it hard to believe, let alone others. And what about the letters? Although not written by her, how could she prove her innocence?
[840] "I need to think," Virginia murmured to herself. "I must think." Who had let him in? It couldn't have been Alice, because if it was, she would have told her right away. The more she thought about it, the more unbelievable the whole thing seemed. There was only one thing to do now - call the police. She reached out to grab the phone, but then thought of George. She needed someone to help her now, someone who could be ordinary in intelligence but cool-headed, able to see the situation from their own perspective and tell her what the best course of action was.
[841] She immediately dismissed the idea of George. He would think of himself first and wouldn't get involved in something like this.
[842] Her expression suddenly softened. She thought of Bill! So she called him right away.
[843] But the person who answered the phone told her that Bill had left for the chimney house half an hour ago.
[844] "Damn it!" Virginia threw down the phone, shouting in frustration. It was terrifying to be alone with a dead body, and no one to talk to.
[845] Just then, the doorbell rang.
[846] Virginia jumped in fright, paused for a moment, and the doorbell rang again.
[847] She knew Alice was upstairs packing, so she couldn't hear the doorbell.
[848] Virginia walked out of the hall, unlatched the safety chain, and opened the bolted door. She sighed deeply and opened the door. Standing in front of her was the young unemployed man.
[849] Virginia's over-tensioned nerves suddenly relaxed.
[850] "Come in," she said. "I think I can give you a job."

[852] "I'm sorry," she said. "I mean... I mean..."

[854] "Pretty much," Virginia agreed.
[855] "I'm in such a state because the conventional fixed jobs just don't suit me. So, I hope, the job I'm offering you is different."
[856] A smile played at the corners of her lips.
[857] "Very different indeed."
[858] "Excellent," the young man said with satisfaction.
[859] Virginia admired his tanned skin and tall frame.
[860] "You see," she explained, "I'm in a difficult position. My friends are all very high up in society. They'll be hesitant."
[861] "I have no concerns, so let's just do it. What's the matter?"
[862] "There's a dead body in the room next door." Virginia said, "He was murdered, and I don't know what to do."
[863] She blurted out these words carelessly, and he remained calm, which increased her admiration for him. He seemed to take these matters in stride, as if they were already familiar to him.
[864] "Excellent." His voice was enthusiastic. "I've always wanted to do some non-professional detective work. Shall we go see the body, or would you like to tell me about it first?"
[865] "I'll give you the background first." She paused to think and organize her thoughts, then calmly and succinctly told him, "This man came to my house yesterday to see me. He brought some letters, love letters, with my signature on them."
[866] "But those letters weren't actually written by you, were they?" the young man said calmly.
[867] Virginia looked at him in surprise. "How did you know?"
[868] "I guessed, you continue."
[869] "He wanted to blackmail me, and I... I don't know if you can understand, but I just went along with it."
[870] "Of course, you wanted to experience that feeling."
[871] "You're so clever," Virginia said. "That's exactly what I was thinking."
[872] "I'm just ordinarily clever," the young man said modestly. "But be careful, not many people can understand this idea, most people wouldn't even think of it."
[873] "Indeed. I let him come back at six o'clock today. When I got home from Ranelagh, I found a fake telegram had been sent, all my servants had been sent away, and there was only one maid left. I went into the study, and there was the man, shot dead."
[874] "Who let him in?"
[875] "I don't know. If it was my maid, she would have told me."
[876] "Does she know about these things?"
[877] "I didn't tell her anything."
[878] The young man nodded and stood up.
[879] "Go and see the body," he said briefly, "but I advise you to tell the truth. Once you tell a lie, you'll have to tell more lies, and then endless lies."
[880] "Are you suggesting I call the police?"
[881] "Perhaps that's best, let's see what that guy has to say first."

[883] "By the way," she said, "you haven't told me your name."
[884] "My name? My name is Anthony Kade."
[885] Chapter Nine: Anthony Disposes of the Body
[886] Anthony followed Virginia out of the room, feeling a bit smug. Things had taken an unexpected turn. But when he bent down to look at the dead man in the chair, his expression grew serious.
[887] "His body is still warm," he said suddenly. "He's been dead for less than half an hour."
[888] "Just before I came in?"
[889] "Yes."

[891] "Did your maid come into this room?"
[892] "No."

[896] "Yes."

[899] Anthony nodded without speaking.
[900] "You're a bit disappointed, aren't you? I get that feeling."
[901] "It's very unfortunate, Mrs. Rue. If you had come home and found this body with your maid, things would have been much simpler. This person was definitely killed before you came back."
[902] "Now someone can say he died after I came back, I understand what you mean."
[903] She immediately understood his meaning, and her reaction confirmed his first impression of her as a beautiful, brave, and wise woman, from the first words she spoke to him on the stairs.
[904] Virginia was so engrossed in the present problem that she didn't find it strange that this stranger knew her name.
[905] "I was wondering why Alice didn't hear the gunshot." she murmured.

[907] "You hear, in London, the sound of a pistol is not too noticeable."

[913] "Well."

[980] The plan went off without a hitch. Anthony took another taxi to the platform and "picked up" the luggage ticket in a timely manner. He had already purchased a used Morris Cowley a few days ago, and he found the car after leaving the platform.
[981] He drove back to Paddington, handed the baggage ticket to the attendant, and the staff retrieved the suitcase from the cloakroom and placed it in the trunk of his car. After everything was in order, Anthony drove away.
[982] His destination was now the outskirts of London. He drove through Notting Hill, Shepherd's Bush, and via Golders Green, then past Brent and Hammersmith, and onto the long stretch of road between Hammersmith and Stein. The road was busy, leaving no footprints or tire marks. Anthony found a place to stop, got out of the car, and used mud to obscure the license plate number. He waited by the side of the road until he couldn't hear any vehicles on either side. He then opened the trunk, pulled out Giuseppe's body, and placed it on the side of the road in a bend where the headlights of passing cars wouldn't shine on it.
[983] He got back in the car and drove away. The entire process took exactly one minute and thirty seconds. He made a right turn and drove back to London via Burnham Woods. After a while, he stopped again and climbed up a large tree. Even for Anthony, this was quite an accomplishment. He hid a small brown paper package in a crevice near the trunk of the tree.
[984] "What a genius way to dispose of the gun," Anthony thought to himself. "Everyone will be looking for it on the ground or in the pond. There aren't many British people who can climb trees."
[985] He then returned to London and Paddington Station, storing the suitcase in another cloakroom at the arrival hall. He was now eager to have a delicious sirloin steak, juicy meat, and a large portion of fries. However, he looked at his watch and sadly shook his head. He filled the Morris with gas and set off again. This time, he headed north.
[986] He parked on the side of the road near the garden of the Chimney House at exactly 11:30. He jumped out of the car and effortlessly scaled the wall, running towards the house. The chimes of a clock could be heard in the distance, indicating that another fifteen minutes had passed.
[987] At 11:45, it was the time mentioned in the note. Anthony had reached the platform in front of the house. He looked up at the darkened building and everything was silent.
[988] "These politicians go to bed so early," he muttered to himself.
[989] Suddenly, a sound entered his ears, a gunshot.
[990] Anthony quickly looked around, the sound had come from inside the house. He waited for a moment, but it was still deathly quiet.
[991] He walked up to a ground-floor window, judging that the gunshot came from this room. He tried the handle, but the window was locked, so he tried other windows. He remained focused on the surrounding noises, but it was still as quiet as ever.
[992] Finally, he began to doubt that the gunshot was imagined by himself or perhaps the sound of someone hunting in the forest. He turned back to the courtyard, feeling a vague sense of dissatisfaction and unease.
[993] He looked back at the house, and suddenly a light came on in one of the second-floor rooms, but it went out in an instant. The place was back to darkness.

[1903] Chapter XVII: Midnight Expedition

[3260] [1] Alphonse Bertillon: A French Parisian clerk in the Identification Department in the 19th century; he developed the first modern system of criminal identification. This system, known as "Bertillonage," consists of three parts: physical measurements, accurate descriptions of the physical characteristics of the suspect, and standardized facial photographs.
